It is clear that the overseas Chinese in Nanyang are filled with righteous indignation about this case and express their extreme sympathy for Ms. Xiao, and can speak out for weak women.

Dr. Zhu Ziyun's Personal Account of His Kidnapping and Escape

Dr. Zhu Personally Appeared in Court Yesterday

Both Defendants Firmly Deny the Charges

The renowned physician Dr. Zhu Ziyun was kidnapped from his residence at 3151 Zhoujiazui Road on September 21st at approximately 10 AM. Harbin Police Detective Zhu Hanbo and French Concession Police Detective Liu Changgen, believing that the Chongming woman Fei Zhu, the landlady of room two at 722 Caihua Lane, Qipu Road, and her husband, Fei Zhenkun, were connected to the bandits and were harboring the kidnap victim, arrested them and brought them before the Special District Court. During interrogation, they denied the accusations and were released on bail of 3,000 yuan each, pending further interrogation when the victim, Zhu Ziyun, appeared in court. This information was previously reported in this newspaper. It is now known that because the two defendants could not secure bail, they remained in custody. Yesterday morning, Judge Ge Zitan of the Third Criminal Court conducted a further hearing. Zhu Ziyun, accompanied by his lawyer, Lu Qi, also appeared in court to provide testimony. Police Lawyer Zhang Tianyin presented the case, stating that Dr. Zhu had arrived in court this morning and requested to be heard. Zhu Ziyun then testified: "At around 10 AM this morning, I was seeing patients at my residence when four bandits suddenly arrived. Two of them rushed in, grabbed my hands, and threatened me with pistols. They forced me outside. One bandit pushed me violently from behind, while another stood guard in the courtyard. I was forced into a car that they had pre-arranged. My head struck the car window, and I became dazed. However, I vaguely remember the route. We turned off Yalu Road, went through Peng Road, and then entered Caihua Lane, where I was held temporarily on the upper floor of a certain building. We entered through the back door. Two bandits were assigned to guard me that evening. There was a Shaoxing woman, about twenty years old, who was in charge of bringing meals. I saw this woman standing at the door when I entered the bandit's den. I have never seen the two defendants before, but I heard them speaking with a Chongming accent, and they were calling for mahjong downstairs. The bandits all spoke with Jiangbei Shaoxing accents. One had a pockmarked face and wore Western clothes, and there was one female bandit (the one who delivered meals). At three o'clock the next morning, they moved me to a small boat in a secluded river in the French Concession. Two bandits took turns guarding me, each with a pistol. They did not ask me to write a letter to my family demanding ransom. After several days on the bandit boat, I became somewhat familiar with the bandits guarding me. I casually asked them if they were the leaders. They said that the leaders were all regimental commanders and brigade commanders, and they were hired by them, earning a monthly salary of thirty yuan. Later, I tried to persuade them with kind words, saying, 'If you want to be comrades, why not join the army? Furthermore, your leaders are mistaken in thinking I am a wealthy man. I am just a doctor and have no savings. If the police were to catch you, you would be in great danger. I currently have sixty gold coins on my person. Could I give them to you temporarily in exchange for my release? I will give you a reward of five hundred yuan later, and I will not go back on my word.' The bandits seemed to understand what I was saying. On the 28th, they released me. I immediately returned home. They have not come to collect the five hundred gold coins to this day. I reported it to the police, and that evening, I went with detectives to Qipu Road to try and identify the bandit's den, but I couldn't find it. The next morning, I went again with the detectives and recognized the location where the two defendants lived. I had previously received threatening letters from the bandits demanding money, but I ignored them." Detective Zhu then testified that the extortion letters, two in total, were now in the police's possession. One demanded three thousand yuan, and the other demanded one thousand yuan, and they arranged to meet at the Tianhou Temple Bridge, among other things. Judge Ge verified the testimony and questioned the two defendants, who firmly denied the accusations. He then ordered them to be remanded in custody separately, pending a further hearing at a later date.

Three Homicide Cases in Western Shanghai

Burning...Bullet Wounds...Murder

Worshipping Gods and Thanking Buddha Leads to the Burning of a Sick Child. Ding Shaoqing, a farmer residing at 14 Nanjie Street, Hongqiao Town, Western Shanghai, is over seventy years old. He has only one son, named Genxin, who is fifteen years old and learning the lacquer trade. Shaoqing loves him like the apple of his eye. However, on the third of this month, Genxin suddenly fell seriously ill with typhoid fever. In addition to seeking medical treatment, the night before last, he specially invited two Taibao (a superstitious practice that is now prohibited) to his home to worship gods and thank Buddha, and went to the temple to "invite joy" (requiring seven lanterns) and perform various superstitious acts. At around two o'clock yesterday morning, the lantern hanging over the patient's bed, used for "inviting joy," suddenly caught fire, causing the bed curtains to ignite. At that time, Shaoqing and his wife were cooking tea downstairs. The only person in the upstairs room was Genxin, who was lying sick in bed. The Taibao and others had already left after completing their tasks. By the time Shaoqing brought the tea upstairs, the room was filled with flames. He attempted to save his beloved son twice, but was unable to enter. On the third attempt, he finally managed to rescue him, but Genxin had already been burned all over his body, with no intact skin. The scene was gruesome and unbearable to witness. He succumbed to his injuries and died yesterday morning. Shaoqing and his wife, seeing their beloved son dead, were overcome with grief. Tears streamed down their faces, and they repeatedly fainted. The family has now reported the incident to the Wangjialou Police Station of the First Branch of the Sixth District, requesting exemption from an autopsy and arranging for the burial themselves.

Accidental Discharge of a Bullet Kills a Colleague. Lei Zaiyin, a third-class police officer at the Longhua Substation of the Third Branch of the Sixth District of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, was from Dehua, Jiangxi, and was twenty-three years old. Wang Genglin, from Changshu, was thirty-three years old. The two had a very good relationship. At around ten o'clock the night before last, Lei, Wang, and Zhang Shijun were ordered to escort a thief to the Caohejing station. They then patrolled the area around the Shanghai-Hangzhou Road until 2:15 AM yesterday morning, when they returned to the Longhua Substation. Wang Genglin returned one or two minutes earlier. By the time Lei and Zhang returned to the bedroom, Wang was already sitting on the bunk on the west side. Lei Zaiyin, who was lying on the opposite side, had just unloaded four bullets from the rifle he was carrying, leaving one bullet inside, which he forgot about. As Officer Lei was about to hang the rifle on the wall, he accidentally touched the trigger with his finger. The bullet suddenly fired and struck Wang Genglin in the chest, who was resting on the opposite bunk. The bullet exited through his back, and he fell onto the bunk, dying instantly. A hole was also pierced in the wall. Lei, seeing the tragedy he had caused, was overcome with grief and attempted to shoot himself in the throat with the rifle, wishing to die as atonement. Fortunately, Zhang Shijun saw this and rushed to snatch the gun away. After investigation, Inspector Jia detained Lei and sent him to the Third Branch of the Sixth District, and then to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for questioning. He also telegraphed Wang's family in Shanghai and reported the incident to the local court for an autopsy. Yesterday, the court sent Prosecutor Zhao, along with a forensic examiner, to confirm that the death was accidental. He ordered a coffin to be prepared for burial, pending further investigation.

A Murdered Male Corpse Discovered in a Wasteland. A murdered male corpse was discovered in the reeds in the southeast corner of the Magenlang area, number sixteen map, twenty-eighth Bao, south of Hongqiao Road, Western Shanghai (the area bordering the First and Second Branches of the Sixth District, very close to Zhongshan Road). A farmer saw it while cutting grass in the field and reported it to the Wangjialou Police Station of the First Branch of the Sixth District. Chief Chen of the patrol considered the area to be under the jurisdiction of the Second Branch of the Sixth District and immediately notified the Heyoujiao Police Station. Patrol Chief Li Huapu, upon receiving the report, went to inspect the corpse. The corpse was approximately twenty years old, with a naked upper body, wearing only white cotton shorts and yellow silk socks, without shoes. The hair was very long. The skull was shattered, the face was covered in blood, and the whole body was bruised. There were deep rope marks around the neck and abdomen. No family members came to claim the body. Chief Li immediately ordered the head of the local area, Shen Yunpu, to report the case to the local court for an autopsy, pending a thorough investigation and arrest of the perpetrator.

Yu Jingyu's Appeal Rejected

Yu Jingyu of Haimen, acting as a member of the 20th sub-division of the second district, sued Wu Jianguang, Wang Zhenhai, Wang Yonghai, and the sons of the deceased Chai Wenzhong, Cai Gao and Cai Fa, astrologer of having made false and deceptive accusations and fraud for financial gain in the Special District Court. In the initial trial, all five defendants were found not guilty. Yu appealed the verdict to the collegiate bench. Following the conclusion of interrogations, Judge Xu Jiashi, along with Assessors Sun Yuan and Ge Zitan, ascended the bench in the First Criminal Court yesterday afternoon. Only the defendant Wu Jianguang was present; the plaintiff Yu Jingyu and the remaining defendants were absent. Judge Xu then announced the verdict, rejecting the appeal.

The Wharf Management Office Streamlines City Docks

Expelling Gangs: Ensuring Traveler Safety

The Nanshi Wharf Management Office of the Shanghai Port Authority has made considerable efforts to streamline the Nanshi area wharfs. Since the Port Authority took over the Chaonan Wharf at the 16th Bund, a patrol team has been stationed there, dedicated to protecting merchants and travelers at the wharfs and eliminating old malpractices. The six-gang party, the eight-gang party, the sixteen-gang party, the thirty-two-gang party, the seventy-two-gang party, all of whom relied on the wharfs for survival, have all been expelled. Each time a ship docks, the patrol team is stationed on the shore, prohibiting anyone from standing on the wharf until the passengers have disembarked. Only then are porters allowed to board the ship to transport goods, following regulations and maintaining order, with no discrepancies or thefts occurring. Merchants and travelers alike applaud this achievement, marking a new era for Chinese ports. According to Xu Shichuan, the director of the Nanshi Wharf Management Office, and Gao Erde, the leader of the patrol team, efforts will be made to improve the Nanshi area wharfs to create a model wharf for the entire country.

The Fuqing Steamer Case Concludes with Release

The Fuqing steamer of the Fuxing Company, which originally operated the Xinghua-Quanzhou route, was previously involved in a lawsuit due to financial disputes at the management office. The Jianghai Customs was ordered to detain the steamer pending the legal proceedings. Since the Fuqing steamer was detained, it had been out of service for a long time. The lawsuit concluded yesterday with a ruling to release the ship and allow it to resume operations as usual. Yesterday afternoon, the Fuxing Company requested the Shanghai Customs to release the Fuqing steamer, which the Customs granted, immediately ordering its release. The company is preparing to resume its Xinghua route.

The Hongkou Epidemic Hospital Closes

Decision to Raise Funds to Build a Building

The Hongkou Epidemic Hospital has been in operation since July of this year. Initially, it was relatively quiet, but unexpectedly, the epidemic intensified in the autumn. The first person in Shanghai diagnosed with true cholera (Xia Fugou) was examined by the hospital. The situation was extremely dangerous, but he was successfully cured. The hospital has a good track record, saving countless lives. Recently, due to the cool weather, the epidemic has subsided. The hospital officially announced its closure yesterday and held a concluding meeting. The meeting was chaired by the medical director, who reported that the epidemic was mild in the summer but intensified in the autumn. A total of over 2,600 people received treatment, an increase of one-third compared to previous years. Among them, only twenty-five people were diagnosed with true cholera, all of whom were successfully cured and discharged. The hospital has repeatedly received plaques and newspaper acknowledgments from grateful patients. The Municipal Health Bureau has also sent staff to visit and provide guidance daily, expressing satisfaction. The administrative director then reported a summary of income and expenses, stating that Hongkou is a semi-industrial area, and most residents are poor. The hospital has been operating for three terms. Given the increasing number of patients seeking treatment each year, and the hospital's land has been purchased and drawings have been made, there is an urgent need to build a hospital building to avoid the annual cost of building reed sheds and thatched huts (six to seven hundred yuan) and the inconvenience and losses of storing items here and there. After lengthy discussions, it was decided that the directors would first raise funds for the construction of the building. If a certain amount is raised, another meeting will be held to discuss the progress.

Rickshaw Pullers Complain of Hardship

Meng Jinchen and other representatives of rickshaw pullers in Zhabei stated that life has become increasingly difficult in recent years. Renting rickshaws is a hardship, and their earnings are meager. The rickshaw owners are unsympathetic and want to increase the rent by ten cents. Some people even plan to monopolize the rickshaws in the name of public associations, which is intolerable to the rickshaw pullers. They have drafted a declaration and sent it to various organizations and groups, requesting assistance.

The Water Police Conference to Combat Pirates

Eight Resolutions Passed

The commander of the fourth district of the Wusong Maritime Public Security Team of the Province of Jiangsu noted the rampant piracy off the coast of Wusong, with frequent incidents of kidnapping and looting, affecting maritime security. He convened a district affairs meeting at the district headquarters at 2 PM yesterday afternoon, summoning the commanders of the sixteen team, Chen Xin; the seventeen team, Gong Mianqin; the eighteen team, Lin Cha; and the chief of the general affairs section, Wu Gengyang. Commander Zhang chaired the meeting. The resolutions passed are recorded below: (1) Increase the number of police officers in each team; (2) Eliminate the old and weak officers; (3) Replenish firearms and distribute them to each team to strengthen their forces; (4) Repair any damaged patrol boats in each team promptly; (5) Add patrol boats to teams with large patrol areas to facilitate deployment; (6) The pirates in the waters around Chongqi Tongru Sea appear and disappear unpredictably and have recently landed and looted, which is extremely illegal. The commanders of the sixteen, seventeen, and eighteen teams will supervise their respective platoon leaders to earnestly patrol and suppress pirates in their respective areas; (7) Organize a detective team to specifically investigate the whereabouts of pirates in order to ensure their suppression; (8) Reorganize the patrol areas of the major teams and their respective platoons, formulate plans, and submit them to the provincial department for approval and implementation. The meeting adjourned after the resolutions were passed.

Negotiations to Stop Disrupting the Price of Almond Shao

Ling Yongde will File a Lawsuit

Recently, the Mid-Autumn Festival was celebrated according to the lunar calendar. People in society, unable to break old customs, still gave each other domestic almond shao as gifts. Therefore, there were many buyers on that day. Among them, a customer went to Yihe Garden to buy wine and was greatly dissatisfied after inquiring about the price. He said, "We are going out of our way to come here, wanting to get a little discount. Now, your factory's own product is more expensive than the one sold on the market by five cents. That is extremely unfair." Ling Yongde, the factory owner, heard this and, believing that it was related to the future of the business, immediately treated the customer with courtesy and asked about the truth. He learned that the Taichang Wine Store on Fada Road also sold the same wine. He was deeply concerned that unscrupulous merchants were imitating it, so he went there to investigate the truth. Later, he saw that the wine being sold was indeed a product of his factory. He asked a fellow partner at Taixing, who said that the retail price for small-scale almond shao on the market was 25 cents, while this store only sold it for 20 cents. When asked about the source, he said it was delivered by a manager surnamed Hu. Ling had no choice but to return to the factory to check the books. There was no wholesale shipment to Taixing. At this point, he filed a report with the Yangshupu Police Station, requesting an investigation. After receiving the report, the police chief, considering the case to be related to the credibility of the business community, and noting that the store dared to privately receive goods from an unknown source, and sold them at a lower price, which was highly suspicious, immediately ordered Detective Ge Futing, Wang Tongpo, and a foreign detective to go to the French Concession Police Station, report the situation, and then go together to the Taixing Wine Store at 371 Fada Road to confiscate the stolen wine and several declaration letters and brochures. They took them back to the police station for safekeeping. It is now known that Ling Yongde, the manager of Yihe Garden, believes that Wu Baolian, the manager of Taixing Wine Store, should not have undermined the industry by disrupting the selling price of products. He is said to be filing a criminal lawsuit, requesting the court to handle the matter according to law.

The Wusong Jide Charity Hall's Re-election Fails

The Wusong Jide Charity Hall was established in the eighth year of the Daoguang era of the Qing Dynasty. Recently, due to poor management, it was reported to the Social Bureau by local people. At the same time, the candidates were notified to attend the re-election at the Wusong Municipal Office on the afternoon of the seventh. Unexpectedly, on the morning of the day before yesterday, Qiangsheng, a special representative sent by the Social Bureau, went to Song and went to the hall, saying that among the candidates submitted for this re-election, it was found that seven or eight people, including Yu Weigan, had either bad habits, misappropriated public funds, or been subjected to administrative penalties. Therefore, this re-election was deemed inappropriate and was ordered to be suspended temporarily. The list of local gentry and merchants should first be submitted to the Social Bureau for approval before scheduling a new date for the re-election. Yu Weigan, the former executive director of the hall, also claimed illness and did not attend, so there was no way to contact him. After Liu Youtong of the Municipal Administration Bureau informed him of the details, he returned to Shanghai to report the situation.

The New Italian Consul General Will Arrive in Shanghai

Count Ziano: Expected to Arrive on Double Tenth Day

The newly appointed Italian Consul General to Shanghai, Count Ziano (son of the Italian Minister of Communications), and his wife, Edda (eldest daughter of Italian Prime Minister Mussolini), departed from Rome at 10:40 PM on September 9th, heading to Brindisi (an Italian port on the southeast coast) to board the Lloyd Triestino's De Fore (Tevere). They are expected to arrive in Shanghai around October 10th. Those who saw them off at the Rome station, in addition to Prime Minister Mussolini and Minister of Communications Ziano, included various dignitaries from the Fascist Party and the political world, senior officials from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and others. Zhu Shuangzhai, the secretary of the Chinese Legation in Italy, also went to the station to greet them and presented Countess Ziano with a bouquet of flowers, wishing them a safe journey. The Countess shook hands and thanked him before boarding the train.

Count Ziano was born in Livorno on March 18, 1903. He graduated from the Faculty of Law at the University of Rome on April 20, 1922. On July 21, 1925, he passed the diplomatic and consular examinations and began studying at the Ministry. He was later assigned to the Brazilian Legation as a trainee. On January 10, 1929, he was awarded the Italian Crown Order, Fifth Class. On April 30, 1926, he was promoted to attaché at the Legation. On June 19, 1926, he was transferred to the Argentine Legation. On March 14, 1927, he returned to the Ministry to work. On April 1, 1927, he was promoted to deputy secretary of the Legation. On May 16, 1927, he was transferred to the Legation in Beiping, promoted to first-class deputy consul with the title of Legation Secretary. On April 31, 1929, he was promoted to third-class consul, retaining his position as Legation Secretary. On June 25, 1929, he was appointed secretary to the Italian Embassy to the Holy See. On April 21, 1930, he was awarded the Italian Crown Order, Fourth Class. On May 31, 1930, he was appointed Italian Consul General to Shanghai, succeeding Count Anna. He is only twenty-seven years old, has traveled to South America and the Far East, and has an excellent record of service at the Ministry and Legation. He is extremely intelligent and hardworking, a rare talent among young people. His wife has been to India and Egypt and graduated from the Fuliansi Girls' School in Italy, R·Istituto della S·S·AnnunsiataaFrienza, a school known for its noble women. She excels in sports such as playing ball and horse riding. In Rome, she often rode horses in the park with her father. The U.S. Prime Minister Mussolini sent his fast son-in-law to China, and we can see that he attach great importance to China, since China is a new country, sending young element who has a new idea to the extent the economic relations between Italy and China. We deeply hope the economic relation will continue to become political cooperation.

The South Vietnamese Chinese General Chamber of Commerce Requests Joint Resistance Against the Harsh Passport Law

Willing to Back the Chinese Overseas Federation

The Chinese Overseas Federation received a telegram from the South Vietnamese Chinese General Chamber of Commerce yesterday: "To the Shanghai Chinese Republic Chinese Overseas Federation, respectfully, we received your respectful telegram. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs' promulgation of measures for issuing passports and temporary measures for issuing return passports and visas for foreigners coming to China, stipulating a fee of six yuan per passport and two yuan for stamps, with annual renewal and payment, is a harsh and cumbersome law that is unprecedented in ancient and modern times. It makes it difficult for overseas Chinese to endure. Overseas Chinese abroad are forced to make a living abroad due to the poverty of their motherland, enduring unequal treatment from foreigners and bearing heavy taxes from foreigners. We hope that the government of the motherland can help alleviate our suffering. Unexpectedly, the government has done the opposite. The so-called revolutionary diplomacy implemented by the government in recent years to amend treaties has not brought any benefit to overseas Chinese. Instead, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has taken the opportunity to implement measures for paying high fees for passports, greatly increasing the suffering of overseas Chinese. How can overseas Chinese not be disheartened by this? The Ministry of Foreign Affairs' harsh treatment of overseas Chinese and its exploitation of overseas Chinese is almost worse than what overseas Chinese receive from foreigners. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs is like a butcher, and overseas Chinese are like fish on the chopping board. How much blood and sweat do overseas Chinese have? We are already groaning under the oppression of foreigners and have not received the help of our country. How can we have the strength to fill the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' insatiable desires and meet its greedy demands? Most of the overseas Chinese here are poor and powerless, paying large amounts of head taxes and various heavy taxes to foreigners every year. There are often those who cannot pay and are deported. Suddenly, upon hearing of this harsh law, we were extremely agitated, and the people are in uproar. In addition to submitting another report to the Central Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee to forward it to the National Government, requesting the abolition of this harsh law by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, we respectfully request that your Federation earnestly uphold the interests of all overseas Chinese and represent the public opinion of all overseas Chinese, continuing the struggle to the end. Our Chamber of Commerce respectfully represents all the overseas Chinese in Vietnam to be your backing. The Vietnamese Chinese General Chamber of Commerce bows, with cold seal. It is heard that the Chinese Overseas Federation will ask the government for approval of its request, ordering the Ministry of Finance and the two provincial governments of Guangdong and Guangxi to remit 100,000 yuan to relieve the victims of the Kunxiong fire, and that the Relief Committee will also remit 10,000 yuan, which shows that the government has not forgotten the overseas Chinese. The harsh passport law privately enacted by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs is hated by the entire overseas Chinese community, and the government will certainly be able to consider the public opinion of all overseas Chinese and abolish the law. We plan to work together to appeal again, to alleviate the difficulties of the Soviet overseas Chinese."

Revised Regulations on Handling Fees at the Jianghai Customs

Effective October 7th, the old regulations of the Jianghai Customs, including the measurement and inspection procedures for unloading goods from foreign and inland river steamers, have been in place for over sixty years. Now, with the approval of the Superintendent of Customs upon submission by the Inspector General of Customs, new regulations have been revised and implemented starting yesterday. Detailed regulations on the collection of all handling fees are posted inside the customs office. Various shipping companies and customs brokers can request copies for review. Recent News on the Negotiation Regarding the Sinking of the "Xin Kang"

The family association of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's "Xin Kang" steamer, which was sunk by the Japanese Mail Steamship Company's "Tatsuno Maru" on July 21st last year in the waters off Chengshan Cape in Shandong, resulting in the drowning of many people and the loss of millions of dollars in property, held a meeting the other day. To date, it has been over a year, and the China Merchants Bureau and the bereaved family association have repeatedly telegraphed the National Government, requesting serious negotiations. However, due to the Japanese side's lack of sincerity, there have been no results whatsoever. Subsequently, the China Merchants Bureau's diplomatic approach failed to resolve the matter. Therefore, they submitted a request to the Ministry of Communications for approval to proceed legally in accordance with international practice. They have already filed a lawsuit with the Shanghai Special District Local Court. The bereaved family association has also taken steps to achieve the goal of consoling the deceased and providing for the living. They have already hired Sheng Zhen as their lawyer to act as their litigation agent and have filed a lawsuit with the Special District Court. However, due to litigation costs, the formal submission of the petition has not yet occurred. They are currently applying for financial assistance. The bereaved family association specifically convened a committee meeting the other day to discuss litigation issues. Standing Committee Member Mr. Zhu reported on the association's affairs. Following this, the matter of pursuing litigation was discussed. It was stated that all litigation procedures and evidence lists were complete. However, due to a lack of funds, they could not proceed. As this concerns national rights and the lives of the people, they should request assistance from the court. A resolution was passed to this effect, and Committees Zhu and Zhou were appointed to negotiate all matters with Lawyer Sheng. Next, the issue of providing relief to impoverished families facing livelihood difficulties was discussed. It was resolved to negotiate with the China Merchants Bureau for an allocation of funds for relief. The issue of the association's finances was not discussed. Due to financial difficulties, there are issues regarding the operation of the association. The various committee members will find ways to maintain the association. Finally, other association affairs were discussed before the meeting adjourned.

Letter from the Anti-Opium Society to All Anti-Opium Comrades Nationwide

The 7th Anti-Opium Movement Week Concludes. The 7th National Anti-Opium Movement Week has been held for a week. The enthusiasm of the movement in this city and other places has been detailed in various newspapers. The China National Anti-Opium Society, in order to request anti-opium organizations and enthusiastic individuals to continue their efforts in the anti-opium movement, specifically records its letter to comrades of all anti-opium organizations as follows:

All Comrades of National Anti-Opium Organizations, Greetings: The 7th National Anti-Opium Movement Week has concluded. Looking back on the movement during this week, it originated in Shanghai and spread throughout the north, south, east, and west of the country, reaching far and wide. Although there are certainly cases where the interior was unable to hold events consistently due to the impact of military affairs or political instability, those who participated in the movement still covered the entire country, and the situation was increasingly enthusiastic. This shows that those who advocate for opium prohibition share the same heart and the same principle, which cannot be suppressed by any force. With every fraction of development in public opinion, the hope for opium prohibition increases by a fraction. We have been hoarse and exhausted from engaging in the anti-opium movement, yet the scourge of opium has been rampant and has not been eliminated, which is inevitably disheartening. However, our efforts should not be swayed by success or failure. We must set a firm goal and make persistent efforts to achieve success. Today, the Anti-Opium Movement Week has concluded, but the anti-opium movement does not end with it. We should expand the scope, extend the time, promote the spirit of Anti-Opium Week, and continue the work of Anti-Opium Week. With a spirit of fearlessness, we will engage in a movement to save the country. The main points announced during this Anti-Opium Week are all the only correct path for our work. If we want to wash away national humiliation, we must first reject opium. If we want to talk about opium prohibition, we must emphasize abiding by the law. Other aspects, such as improving families and strengthening physiques, should also eliminate the harm of opium. Eliminating famine to enrich the people's food also requires eliminating opium seedlings all over the land. National wealth and a strong populace are closely related to the success or failure of opium prohibition. This is the principle of anti-opium and also the key to saving the country. Our association uses the combination of the people to create an invincible shield of public opinion. We are willing to use our position as representatives of the people to offer sincere advice to the authorities, earnestly ensuring that this dying opportunity can have hope of revival. The people would be fortunate, the country would be fortunate. The China National Anti-Opium Society humbly announces.

Extension of Wheat Stock Registration Deadline

Extended to the 12th of October. The Shanghai Agricultural Products Inspection Institute originally set the deadline for the registration of wheat stocks in Shanghai from October 1st to October 5th. It is now reported that the Shanghai Chinese Grain, Oil, and Cake Traders Association sent a letter to the Institute, stating that most of the wheat in stock belongs to customers and requires a detailed investigation that cannot be completed urgently. They requested a one-week extension for convenient processing. The Institute replied to the Association, agreeing to extend the deadline to October 12th. Wheat merchants must complete the registration of all stocks before October 12th. From October 13th, regardless of old or new arrivals, all stocks will be treated as new goods and subject to inspection and verification in accordance with the provisional measures for wheat inspection.

Extension for Supplementary Inspection of Prepared Medicines

The Ministry of Health has approved a further six-month extension. The Municipal Government received a dispatch from the Ministry of Health yesterday, stating that Article 5 of the Regulations for the Administration of Prepared Medicines stipulates that "all prepared medicines sold before the implementation of these regulations must, within six months of implementation, apply for supplementary inspection and obtain a permit in accordance with Article 2." The dispatch acknowledges that the procedures for amending medicine inserts and prescriptions, as well as printing, are complex and cannot be completed in a short time. After careful verification by the Ministry, the situation is deemed to be true. In order to consider the difficulties faced by various medicine merchants, it has been approved that after the original deadline in Article 5 of the regulations has expired, a further six-month extension will be granted, until April 26th, 1931, to show consideration. The dispatch requests that the Municipal Government investigate and instruct its subordinates to comply accordingly. It is reported that the Municipal Government immediately instructed the Health Bureau to comply and inform the various medicine merchants, as well as instructing the Public Security and Social Affairs Bureaus to be informed.

Notice to Preparatory Party Members Leaving Shanghai

There is a flexible method for taking the oath and receiving certificates. The Organization Department of the Shanghai Special Municipal Executive Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang issued a notice to the various Party branches in the city yesterday, stating: For the purpose of notification, recently, a small number of preparatory Party members have left Shanghai for other places due to circumstances, making it difficult for them to take the oath and receive certificates, which creates difficulties for their Party membership. Therefore, this Department has specifically formulated three flexible measures for preparatory Party members leaving Shanghai to take the oath and receive certificates. These measures have been submitted to the Central Organization Department for approval and filing. In addition to distributing and publishing the notice, the measures are copied and distributed to all, so that they may be known and followed. It is essential that they be followed and that subordinate preparatory Party members be instructed to comply accordingly. This notice is given. The flexible measures for preparatory Party members leaving Shanghai to take the oath and receive certificates are as follows: 1. If a preparatory Party member has completed the Party membership procedures in this city but has not yet been issued a certificate and leaves Shanghai due to circumstances, they should report in detail to the district branch where they completed the Party membership procedures: "Reasons for leaving Shanghai," "Location of destination," "Name, detailed address, and names of standing committee members of the Party branch near the destination." 2. After receiving the report, the district branch will submit it to this Department through successive levels. After verification by this Department, the certificate and oath will be mailed to the Party branch at the member's destination. The Party branch will notify the member to take the oath and receive the certificate in accordance with the Preparatory Party Member Oath Regulations. 3. After the member has taken the oath and received the certificate, the Party branch at the destination should send the oath and a report on the oath-taking situation back to this Department.

Bride Falls from Sedan Chair

Pedestrian Beaten by Crowd

Pei Gong, a Funing native residing at 5 Tanzhiwan, Zhabei, took a wife yesterday. At around 3:30 p.m., after receiving the bride, they proceeded along the north end of Tanzhi Road to the groom's residence for the ceremony. Midway, a group of over twenty men stopped the sedan chair, determined to see the bride. At that time, there were many people and much noise. Suddenly, a shout of "fight" erupted, and over ten people engaged in fighting, causing the sedan chair to overturn, greatly frightening the bride. An Old Man's Son Dies Under a Car

Wu Guanrong, only Six Years Old. Wu Amao, a local resident of 61 Yuqing Lane, Xixinqiao Street, French Concession, was fifty-one years old and had only one son, Guanrong, who was just six years old. At 11:00 a.m. the day before yesterday, Wu's child and a neighboring child (about ten years old) were playing and chasing each other in the street. As the two children were running, a car driven by Feng Amao, license number 11823, came along. Wu's child was unable to avoid it and was knocked down and injured. The police arrived, recorded the license number, and sent the injured child to Renji Hospital for treatment. They also reported back to the police station. The child, Wu, died shortly after being admitted to the hospital due to serious injuries. The hospital notified the police, who transported the body to the Tongren Fuyuantang mortuary. Yesterday morning, the French Concession Car Affairs Office summoned the family of the deceased and the defendant to the French Concession Court. Judge Zhu presided over the examination and confirmed that the child had died from injuries sustained after being hit by a car. After Judge Zhu questioned the defendant, he ordered photographs to be taken and the family of the deceased to claim the body for burial.

Deadline for retrieval is February of Next Year. It was taken over a few days ago in preparation for relocation. However, there are more than 800 coffins temporarily placed in Wumu Garden, which makes transportation difficult. It is hereby notified that the Suzhou Wumu Garden Guixiang Jingshe base and buildings have been allocated to this school by the Ministry of Communications for running the school and were officially taken over on August 7th of this year. All coffins and longevity boards temporarily placed in the garden should be moved as soon as possible. The Wuxian County Government has issued a notice that the family members of the coffins must take them all out by the end of February of the 20th year of the Republic of China. No delays are allowed. If there are unclaimed coffins without owners that are not claimed after the deadline, this school will be responsible for burying them. The owners of the coffins are requested to come to the new campus preparation office of this school at the ancient Wumu Garden to discuss the matter. Cui Yi, Owner of the Cui Clan's Banxiangting

Guidelines for Social News Submissions

(1) Articles should concern domestic and international science, industry, commerce, rural areas.

(2) Items concerning health, aviation, exploration, customs, or urban life are also acceptable. Books are limited to lyrical works related to social life.

(3) Photographs of seasonal events, scenery, flora and fauna, people, and news-related photography are acceptable. Photographs of beautiful women in seasonal or scenic settings are especially welcome.

(4) The length of each article should not exceed two thousand words.

(5) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(6) Do not write the manuscript horizontally, and do not write carelessly. Western text should be avoided where possible. If it is absolutely necessary to quote the original text, it must be included below the translation.

(7) Do not use blue ink for drawings, and do not use colored paper. Use white paper and black ink.

(8) Please indicate "Social News Editorial Department" on the submitted manuscript.

(9) Submitted manuscripts will not be returned, whether published or not. If you require a return, you must state this in advance.

(10) Remuneration for articles is divided into three levels: three yuan, two yuan, and one yuan per thousand words. The same applies to books and photographs per item. Special articles will be compensated separately.

Youth Corner

Saturday - Hongkou Park

— Kui En

On a Saturday afternoon, everything seems to be vibrant, especially Hongkou Park, which is close to the city but still retains its natural beauty. It further reveals how people, weary from the busyness of life, have an even greater interest in nature. Their emotions are very intense and lively, yet very natural. The verdant grass is covered by a cerulean sky. The trees planted around the lawn seem to be resting without moving. Although there is a gentle breeze with warm sunlight from time to time, it only sways slightly, shakes a few times, and then drops a few yellow leaves to avoid spoiling the breeze's mood. This is a day near the Mid-Autumn Festival in the lunar calendar. Because of the fierce, chilling winds that have been blowing for days, some people are hibernating at home, others are busy with the work they must do to make a living, and friends with nothing to do would rather spend a few cents to go to the movies. Who would be willing to appreciate the bleak autumn scenery? But today is different. The chilling wind has turned into a gentle and lovely breeze. A large crowd of people is moving around in the park, which is enough to show that people's interest is particularly strong today.

Qin's nature is very fond of nature, so every day she has to spend a few copper coins to take the tram to Hongkou Park, which is two or three miles away, to breathe some fresh air and appreciate some natural scenery. Today's beauty, of course, cannot be an exception for her.

She always goes to the park alone. She especially does not like to go with friends of the opposite sex, because she is most afraid of being stared at by others with strange eyes, which is not as free as being alone. She likes to quietly appreciate the natural scenery, the chirping of insects and birds, the leaping of fish in the water, ... everything ... is good material for her to enjoy alone. She grew up in the countryside, so she is very attentive to those Japanese people fishing and to the fact that they have this special right.

Because she likes fishing the most. She often stands next to them watching them fish. Her eyes are very focused on the mark on the fishing rod line. As long as that mark moves slightly, she knows that a fish has come to eat the bait. At that time, her emotions are very tense, and her heart is beating. However, when the Japanese fisherman very casually pulls up his fishing rod, it disappoints her again. She despises the clumsiness of the Japanese and their inability to fish. She recalls how well she used to fish when she lived in the countryside, how she held many fish in her hands on the way home, thinking about how happy her family would be when they saw how many fish she had caught. She was so surprised that her heart was pounding, and she could not wait to take three steps at a time to quickly present these many fish to her father, who had the same hobby as her. ... These memories are enough to make her feel that her skills are now itching. Really, the Japanese seem to really not know how to fish. They throw the fragrant bait into the water with a loud thud. She thinks that the fish in the water have long escaped following this huge sound. Where would they come back to eat the bait? The configuration of the fragrant bait, the position of placing the fishing rod, everything is enough to make her feel that the fishing skills of the Japanese are inferior to her. She remembers that Japan is a famous aquatic country, and aquatic products are their major products. Could it be that they only know how to use brutal methods of capture and do not know how to use civilized fishing methods? This is probably the manifestation of the imperialistic characteristics they possess. However, she also thinks that Jiang Taigong's fishing is "those who are willing will be hooked." "The Japanese are fishing or are imitating the ancient culture of our country.

Two Japanese children are playing in front of her. She stares hard at these two Japanese children. She wants to extract from them some model of their so-called imperialism. They are carrying schoolbags, and she is speculating that in the few national textbooks inside, printed with Japanese characters, there must be geography and history subjects. In the history textbook, there is an article explaining how Japan took Manchuria from China. In the geography textbook, there is also a map that includes Manchuria in China's territory into Japan's territory. When a Japanese teacher is lecturing on the podium, how attentively the general little imperial citizens are listening. ... The sound of Japanese soldiers shooting targets outside the park continues to ring incessantly, making her feel that this is not speculation at all but a fact.

It's time for dinner. She is still reluctant to go back, because she feels that life here seems to be particularly meaningful...

Automobile News

Commentary

The New Buick Automobile of 1931

— Ji

After three years of thorough modification and road testing, today's great achievement has been completed. This is the 1931 model of the eight-cylinder New Buick automobile. The new car has many advantages, including an eight-cylinder engine, improved motor, transmission, body, and trim. It is now on display at Buick dealerships across the country for viewing.

For decades, Buick has consistently acted according to its slogan: "Beautiful automobiles, only Buick can make them." Today, the 1931 New Buick adds even more glory to the automobile industry.

Buick engineers have been focusing on research and manufacturing for the past three years, and they firmly believe that the new product of 1931, in terms of all its structures and styles, is indeed the most exquisite and perfect among all cars. Therefore, they dare to present the new product to all sectors of society today.

The new car's motor should be the target of public attention. According to Mr. 克利時, manager of General Motors Corporation in the United States, the new car has been increased to eight cylinders, adding many features. All parts of the car engine have been processed and improved, and the materials have been carefully selected everywhere. It emphasizes both appearance and practicality. This is why Buick automobiles are able to be popular in the world, with two and a half million vehicles driving on roads around the globe every day.

The 1931 New Buick has four types of wheelbases. The wheelbases of models 8-50 are 114 inches, 8-60 are 118 inches, 8-80 are 114 inches, and 8-90 are 132 inches. There are also various convertible and sedan bodies that are spacious and prominent, suitable for various Buick wheelbases, allowing you to choose.

The new cars all have straight-line eight-cylinder, overhead valve engines. The size and power are commensurate with the wheelbase and weight. The 8-50 model uses a bore of 3 7/16 inches and a stroke of 4 1/4 inches to provide power. The displacement area is 220.7 cubic inches, and it can produce 77 horsepower at 3,000 revolutions per minute.

The engine of the 8-60 wheelbase has a bore of 3 1/16 inches and a stroke of 4 5/8 inches. The displacement area is 272.6 cubic inches, and it generates 90 horsepower at 3,000 revolutions per minute.

The engines of the 8-80 and 8-90 wheelbases both have a bore of 3 5/16 inches and a stroke of 5 inches. The displacement area is 344.8 cubic inches, and it generates 104 horsepower at 2,800 revolutions per minute. The capabilities, sturdiness, and durability of the above four types of motors are all extremely superior.

The oil temperature regulator invented by Buick engineers is the first of its kind in automobile mechanical equipment. Engine oil and engine sliding surfaces often lose their effectiveness due to thermal or climatic influences, often expanding and contracting and failing. The advantage of this device is that the engine oil quality does not change, the oil volume does not decrease, and the power is not lost in cold winter or hot summer or under intense driving. The structure is shaped like a small water tank and is in the heat dissipation system between the water pump and the cylinder wall. The oil is ejected from the pump, passes through this gateway, and dissipates when it flows into the engine. In cold weather, the engine oil is frozen and cold. The oil temperature regulator can heat the cold oil and maintain its daily temperature. The heating method relies on the gentle warmth of water vapor and special circulation to allow the oil to flow into the various moving parts of the machine."

Pressure is applied to the general sliding surface, crank journal, connecting rod sliding surface, rocker arm rest, timing gear, and front electrical system sliding surface directly, quickly, and thoroughly. There is also an oil filter and an eccentric ventilation system, each of which constantly keeps the oil quality clean.

The new Buick's eccentric shafts all have five large general sliding surfaces. The force of each shaft is balanced, and the micrometer is inside the eccentric box. The completion is not committed by dirt, which is commonly installed on the outside of the engine. Dirt accumulates and hinders work from time to time.

Buick engineers have learned from three years of testing that combining these five large and strong eccentric shaft tiles with steel ring balancers can save a lot of effort. It can also enlarge the sliding surface area and make it more solid and durable. And its oiling is also the most satisfactory.

Dual carburetor system is available for engines of models 8-65, 8-80 and 8-90. Whether it is a fast car or a slow car, climbing or accelerating, this can obtain super performance. Each carburetor supplies the gasoline to four cylinders. The gasoline is sent from the intake pipe, which is simple, reliable, and exceptionally economical. There is no need to add spark plugs, ignition coils, or other components.

Buick automobiles' valve timing and special air purifiers eliminate all intake noise and produce full power. Buick's overhead valves also make the car run silently. Forged iron pistons are light, strong, and do not shake at all. They will not be damaged after long-term use. The oil flow in the fan shaft is constant. The oil is ejected from the gear pump, which is of course very different from manual oil injectors. The crank driver is a direct gear type.

The transmission box of the new Buick is automatically adjusted and lubricated for long-term use, so there is no need to worry about it often. Only a slight adjustment of the foot pedal is required. Models 8-50 and 8-60 are equipped with single-disc transmission boxes, while models 8-80 and 8-90 are equipped with double-disc transmission boxes, so their heavy duty is also greater.

Gear transmission is a special product of this year's New Buick. Except for the 8-50 model, the other three models have it. This type of setup is mostly only available in high-priced automobiles. Today, the New Buick is both an excellent car and reasonably priced, and it also has the above equipment, which is extremely rare.

This transmission is automatically handled and has no collisions. There is no sound when shifting gears, which is incredibly convenient. It can be used easily at any speed, and its structure is solid and can overcome all kinds of difficulties. In emergencies, such as going uphill or downhill, the gear can be stretched and contracted at any time, and shifting gears is very fast.

The gear transmission is a simple and sturdy organization. It operates directly and does not need to be adjusted. The first speed and reverse gears are standard spiral gears. The gears of the second speed are all aligned on time. The same is true from the first gear to the second gear. The shifting order is not chaotic. Because there are spiral gear transmission boxes and conical friction interconnection mechanisms to control them, collisions are avoided.

Model 8-50 still uses the ordinary three-speed transmission. However, the rotating part of its transmission box is light and small, so its operation is also extremely flexible and without stagnation.

Worm-type and spiral-type driving gears are available for all models except 8-50, and they can be handled on the dashboard. Adding a movable front seat makes driving quite comfortable. The improvement of the car's system is also on par with other features. It is simple and powerful, and the position is spacious. At extremely fast speeds, the mechanical action of the "husband" type car system is very tenacious, reliable, agile, and flexible.

The famous Buick concentrated wheelbase oiling system is still retained. After repeated tests, this system is quite simple and flexible. The oiling work is fast. Because its oil injection mechanism is perfect, each wheelbase sliding surface has an oil pipe connected to it, and the oiling is very thorough without having to go through other parts.

The speed can be as high as 80 miles per hour. You can drive as fast or as slow as you like. It is incomparably stable. It is quiet and silent when driving fast. It is stable on the road. It is extremely reliable whether you are climbing a mountain or going downhill. The acceleration rate of the new engine is about 10 to 60 miles per hour, which is five seconds faster than other cars.

Buick engineers have given deep consideration to speed and have always been conservative and steady. Therefore, high speeds are not easily recommended. The average speed is 70 miles per hour for the 8-50 model, 75 miles per hour for the 8-60 model, and 84 miles per hour for the 8-80 and 8-90 models, which is quite stable.

The new cars all have prominent car bodies. Prominent craftsmanship has always been famous. Therefore, the car bodies and wheelbases of the New Buick are extremely strong and reliable and exquisitely beautiful. The entire frame project is also extremely tenacious and stable.

The interior design and craftsmanship of the New Buick are extremely exquisite, especially magnificent. The quality and color of the呢羢緞布 and edge rope leather are all excellent and beautiful.

The format and position of the car's control instruments are also very commensurate. Driving and riding in between is comfortable and enjoyable. The gear lever and hand brake lever have also been moved to the front, so the driver's leg position is larger than before. The vehicles driving on the right side have also been improved. The hand brake lever is on the left side of the gear lever. The accelerator pedal is quite in line with the position of the foot.

Among the New Buick's mechanical equipment, the most famous are the engine heat meter, water pressure gauge, simultaneous igniter and driver closer, 90-mile speedometer, toe-shaped accelerator pedal, and double-piece vacuum windshield wiper, which are installed on the 8-60, 8-80, and 8-90 sedans. Others are single-piece. Direct and indirect dashboard lights and double-system windshields for convertibles.

Other improvements include four-suspension rubber engine seats, improved water tank seats, new exhaust system, new full-piece rear axle housing, strong frame, new shock absorbers and seats, improved car body seats, new water tank cap, new chrome-plated car top chain nails, complete chrome-plated lighting equipment, new running board inlays and connectors, improved box frames, new driving rudder wheels, new dashboards, rubber-wrapped accelerator pedals, new carpets, and rich and luxurious seats.

89,000-Mile Automobile Honeymoon Trip

— Pei

Goodyear Tires Traverse a Long Distance

Mr. and Mrs. Allen, who live at 139 Ninety-eighth Street in New York, once took a two-year world honeymoon trip by car. They recently returned to the United States from abroad. The situations they encountered during their trip included revolutions, floods, and unbearably hot deserts. The car they used traveled 75,000 miles, and one of the Goodyear tires they prepared traveled as many as 40,000 miles.

Mr. and Mrs. Allen's car is no less than a home. The car has various camping utensils. No matter day or night, the car can be parked anywhere. It can be set up as a kitchen, dining room, and dressing room. In the evening, the cushions in the car can be slightly rearranged to form a comfortable bedroom.

Mr. Allen and Mrs. Allen met on the island of the Philippines and married in China. They set off from Shanghai in March 1928 for their honeymoon. Their total trip totaled 89,000 miles, of which 16,000 miles were spent in China.

The motivation for Mr. and Mrs. Allen to take this long trip is also quite interesting to talk about. The car used for the trip was assembled in China. The car body was made by Chinese people under the direction of Mr. Allen. Mr. Allen said that he found a rudder wheel, so he decided to build a car.

They first took a boat from Shanghai to Manila. After traveling on the island of the Philippines, they took a boat to Singapore, and then drove from Malaya to Penang. After arriving there, they changed boats to Calcutta and drove around India. When the first revolution in Afghanistan broke out, Mr. and Mrs. Allen happened to be driving there at this time. To ensure safety, Mrs. Allen traveled alone by plane. Mr. Allen drove forward on a winding road to avoid the attention of the revolutionaries. Mrs. Allen was arrested by revolutionaries at this time. She was seriously injured in the arm when she escaped. Mr. Allen was shot three times while escaping, which was also very dangerous.

The second thing Mr. and Mrs. Allen experienced was the flood in Kashmir, northwestern India. At that time, the couple was driving for a three-month trip through the Indian desert to Balochistan, and then back to Mumbai. They bought a boat to Aden, Arabia, and then from the Suez Canal to the Red Sea, Cairo in Egypt, and then to Italy, France, 芳的卡羅, England, and finally took the "布蘭加利" boat directly back to their home in New York.

In short, what Mr. and Mrs. Allen experienced was two revolutions in China and one revolution in Afghanistan. Although there was no outbreak in India, the place they went was not far away either. Their honeymoon was not just a trip. They experienced things that travelers had never seen before and made large-scale hunts and visits to Indian kings. The only thing that made Mr. and Mrs. Allen often think of their hometown was that they carried an advertisement for Goodyear tires on their car during their long journey.

Automobile Statistics of Various Countries

— Zhuo

The total number of automobiles in the world has exceeded 24.5 million. The future increase is especially unlimited. The automobile's contribution to shortening the distance on land is truly great. However, the degree of development of transportation industries in various countries is different. The number of automobiles can always reveal the degree of development of the transportation industry. According to the "List of National Conditions of Various Countries" published by the Japan Cabinet Statistics Bureau, the number of automobiles in various countries is listed in detail. We can compare their statistics.

Preparation for Learning to Drive a Car in Vienna

The Vienna Police Department in Austria has recently adopted a "psychological machine" to test prospective car drivers. The illustration shows a test subject concentrating intently, hands on the small steering wheel, carefully guiding a pencil across a map of a heavily congested city street. The cylinder below the map is electrically powered, allowing it to rotate.

Of these, the United States ranks first. The US has a total of 19,954,347 automobiles. England ranks second, France third, and Canada fourth. Although Japan is also known as a major power, it only ranks 21st in the world. Japan only has 35,802 automobiles. As for China, it ranks 35th in the world, with fewer than 14,000 automobiles. The United States has more than 1,700 cars for every 10,000 people, while China has only three cars for every 10,000 people. How underdeveloped is China's automobile industry? Miscellany

Automobile Industry Invents X-Ray Machine

Diagnose Internal Car Problems Instantly

We are already familiar with X-rays for treating human illnesses. But now an X-ray machine has appeared in the automotive industry. Isn't this a wonderful story? This X-ray is specifically designed to diagnose automobile ailments.

The inventor of this car X-ray machine is the Automobile X-Ray Company. The method involves placing a mirror on a stand and connecting it electrically to various components inside the car. Any damage or defects will then appear on the mirror, even the smallest details. The car owner can see it at a glance. Otherwise, when a car breaks down, one is often unaware of the source of the problem, leading to blind searches that take a long time and make repairs impossible, delaying everything. Now, with this mirror, the problem can be identified instantly, which is a great convenience.

This machine weighs 26 pounds, is 3 feet 3 inches tall, and has a circular disk with a diameter of 14 inches. Many American modification companies and car owners are buying these machines to facilitate car maintenance. The benefits of X-rays to the automobile industry are undoubtedly significant.

The machine's disk is decagonal and contains six dials, each with electrical wires connected to a specific component, such as the carburetor and battery. If there is damage, a different phenomenon will appear on the dial. The repairman can then follow the instructions, making it easy to find the problem. The price of each machine is very low. It is currently being sold by the Lewis Brothers Company and will soon be shipped to the Far East for public demonstrations to promote its marvelous functions.
